Who will go down in the annals of history as the next Yokohama Champion? Only time will tell!



Saturday 10:44 p.m. - Top Tables, undefeated after Round 8
----------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
For a wide-open, interesting format like Modern, we try to do full metagame breakdowns of the format to give as accurate a picture as we possibly can. And while that analysis is coming, wading through and breaking down the 1,500 plus deck lists in front of us this weekend is a daunting, time consuming task that can make a man go cross-eyed. Kind of like [Gifts Ungiven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gifts+Ungiven) mirrors.


But we like you. We really do. And so, to whet your appetite for the eventual fountain of data the full analysis will throw your way, we took a trip around the top tables during Round 9 to see what decks were dominating the field this weekend at Yokohama.


And to make sure we only got the best of the best, we stuck to our guns and recorded just the archetypes that are 7-0-1 or better at this point, for a total of 12 decks at the top 6 tables.




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Affinity 2 |
| Jund 2 |
| Melira Pod 1 |
| Naya Pod 1 |
| Splinter Twin 1 |
| White-Black Tokens 1 |
| Martyr of Sands 1 |

Without having seen the full metagame data yet, this list looks pretty representative of the field as a whole, despite its small sample size. The top three decks were pretty clearly three of the most played decks on the weekend (though in what order and by how much, we'll see). All of the lists doing well looked fairly stock, although one did have a pretty spicy [Piracy Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Piracy+Charm) hanging around.



![Piracy Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Piracy+Charm)![Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Snapcaster+Mage)

Of the one-ofs, the [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) and Melira Pod lists were pretty stock, and the Token and Martyr decks, while not commonly played, did not appear to have any major twists or turns to them.


The Naya Pod deck, however, was a sight to behold. Secretly a combo deck ala- [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) , the Naya Pod deck uses either [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) or Village Bell Ringer to combo with [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) , but is able to use cards like [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) and [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) to either provide offense or defense as needed.


What's more, it doesn't look like a combo deck  who combos out in a Red, Green and White deck, after all? In its Round 9 match against the Martyr deck, the Martyr player tapped out facing down just a [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) and Birds of with 38 life. What could go wrong?



![Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker)![Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Restoration+Angel)

The Pod player cast an end of turn [Chord of Calling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chord+of+Calling) for [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) , untapped and cast Kiki-Jiki, copied [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) and was able to cast a second [Chord of Calling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chord+of+Calling) for [Village Bell-Ringer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Village+Bell-Ringer) , winning on the spot.


Yes, winning, which means we'll have the Naya Pod list when we post Day 1 undefeated decks alongside five others.



Round 9 Feature Match - Martin Juza vs. Shouta Yasooka
------------------------------------------------------


*by Chapman Sim*
### Game 1


Both players had already taken two losses so far and would need to win this bubble match if they wanted to compete tomorrow. After winning the die roll, Juza led with [Serum Visions](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serum+Visions) , then further manipulated his library using [Halimar Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Halimar+Depths) before using [Sleight of Hand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sleight+of+Hand) to filter away the unwanted junk.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpyok12/R9_yasooka_VS_juza.jpg)
Yasooka raised everyone's eyebrows when he proceeded to the discard step, pitching [Karn Liberated](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karn+Liberated) . Using this window of opportunity, Juza resolved Deceiver's [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Deceiver%2BExarch), tapping his opponent's only land. Fortunately for Yasooka, he drew [Darkslick Shores](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Darkslick+Shores) the very next turn and used it to cast [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) , ripping [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) from his opponent's hand, cheating death temporarily.



![Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Splinter+Twin)

When Yasooka tried [Thirst for Knowledge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thirst+for+Knowledge) , it was stopped with the first of Juza's [Dispel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispel) s. [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) (countering [Talisman of Dominance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Talisman+of+Dominance) ) and a second Deceiver's [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Deceiver%2BExarch) (used in conjunction) successfully tapped Yasooka out and Juza had a chance to draw [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) for the win.


[Halimar Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Halimar+Depths) showed him [Dispel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispel) and [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) and he could smell the impending win but [Gifts Ungiven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gifts+Ungiven) (granting Yasooka [Condescend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Condescend) and [Go for the Throat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Go+for+the+Throat) ) prevented that from happening so easily.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpyok12/R9_yasooka.jpg)Shouta Yasooka

Yasooka drew his sixth land and passed the turn, keeping up " [Condescend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Condescend) -mana" to stop any of dangerous spells Juza could possibly have. Seeing that Juza had only one card left in his hand, Yasooka slapped [Karn Liberated](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karn+Liberated) onto the board on the very next turn, exiling Deceiver's [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Deceiver%2BExarch). It seemed like the game was over. Juza couldn't deny it and promptly reached for his sideboard.


Martin Juza 0  Shouta Yasooka 1



### Game 2


[Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) was able to remove [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) , but Juza was still armed with [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) and possibly the weekend's most well-represented goblin, [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) .


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpyok12/R9_juza.jpg)Martin Juza

[Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) resolved and Kiki-Jiki hit the bin, leaving Juza with [Serum Visions](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serum+Visions) and Deceiver's [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Deceiver%2BExarch). Yasooka proceeded to tap all his three lands to transmute [Tolaria West](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tolaria+West) , tutoring up [Slaughter Pact](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughter+Pact) for added safety. Now on the receiving end of two attacking Deceiver's [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Deceiver%2BExarch)s, Yasooka was down to just nine life.



![Mindslaver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mindslaver)![Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Spellskite)

Yasooka decided it was time to budge and tried [Gifts Ungiven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gifts+Ungiven) , but Juza was ready with [Negate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Negate) . Now that the countermagic had been baited out, Yasooka untapped, then slammed [Mindslaver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindslaver) onto the board. In a bid to force Yasooka to use [Slaughter Pact](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughter+Pact) , Juza tapped out for Kiki-Jiki. Unable to activate [Mindslaver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindslaver) after paying for the Pact, Yasooka passed the turn, hoping for the best.


Unfortunately for Juza, he had drawn [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) on the turn [Mindslaver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindslaver) had resolved, which meant that Yasooka could wreck havoc on Juza's life total or even kill him instantly if his life total was even. In a bid to stay alive, Juza cracked a fetchland, going down to 17 life, preventing instant death. However, Yasooka flipped a fetchland of the top of Juza's deck, drawing a gasp from the crowd. Shouta Yasooka advances to Day Two and Martin Juza would have to be content touring Japan tomorrow.



Not a combo!


Martin Juza 0  Ken Yukuhiro 2
